    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15667972459375639170">"There is nothing more dangerous...than a character with no author."<br/><br/>*This is the first edtition of The Unwords and it is now out of print. It was only available for a limited number of copies exclusively through the author's official website in 2012. The second edition was published in 2013 by Fearache Publishings and it's available worldwide through all major book retaile</span>
  <span id="freeText15667972459375639170" style="display:none">"There is nothing more dangerous...than a character with no author."<br /><br />*This is the first edtition of The Unwords and it is now out of print. It was only available for a limited number of copies exclusively through the author's official website in 2012. The second edition was published in 2013 by Fearache Publishings and it's available worldwide through all major book retailers in paperback, hardcover, and available exclusively from Amazon in eBook format.*<br /><br />A nameless character. A faceless figure. A disturbing, thought-provoking journey through the facts of the world we live in that we often refuse to acknowledge. <br /><br />The Unwords take full advantage of their author's lack of identity and extreme levels of introspection as they unleash a full scale attack on all fronts of cultural and social decay. <br /><br />Education, religion, politics, language, relationships and common every day social activities are stripped down to their bare foundations and deconstructed through the eyes of a man who considers every act of deceit as an act of war against the people he loves. <br /><br />Poetic verse blends seamlessly with the arts in the form of full page illustrations to create a new, refreshing form of writing the author describes as “Graphic-verse.”<br /><br />Words are meant to be spoken. In a dishonest world, what remains unspoken can only be the truth. In a dishonest world...<br /><br />...the pen is never mightier than the sword.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15667972459375639170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_357531616" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357531616" />
    <a title="Jelena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4245330-jelena"><img alt="Jelena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575808447p2/4245330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/357531616?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jelena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jelena" href="/user/show/4245330-jelena">Jelena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer357531616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5625998569786842539">Mr. John Doe, you are not an unknown person. You are the voice that many should listen to. Imagine you were born couple of centuries ago. Do you think you would live despite the words you're promoting? <br/>I was shocked, don't think I wasn't. The shock came when I realized that you are not a romantic poet, but a rough truth teller. You haven’t given the reflected picture of today’s world, but the true picture of our lives. We build our world on the bloodshed of our ancestors and celebrate it. What’s</span>
  <span id="freeText5625998569786842539" style="display:none">Mr. John Doe, you are not an unknown person. You are the voice that many should listen to. Imagine you were born couple of centuries ago. Do you think you would live despite the words you're promoting? <br />I was shocked, don't think I wasn't. The shock came when I realized that you are not a romantic poet, but a rough truth teller. You haven’t given the reflected picture of today’s world, but the true picture of our lives. We build our world on the bloodshed of our ancestors and celebrate it. What’s to be celebrated? Massacres, homeless hungry people, dead children… One should fight it, not grieve or support through charity organizations. As you said the other day, charity organizations take profit from doing what they’re doing. It’s all about marketing and money. Less production – more telemarketing – that’s today’s economy. A weak individual will see a photograph of an African child and feel guilt. Go to Africa and help the kids, don’t cry over the television commercial of some charity organization. Social crises are made up by the beasts who rule this world behind the closed doors – cowards hiding behind their power and money. They don’t realize that this world doesn’t belong only to them, but to all of us. What they have and we don’t is the ability to kill and sleep peacefully afterwards. They can say a single word and others will obey. We can shout and we will be silenced.<br />I like the “Shhhh” God – the Crucified One. An excellent technique and the symbol of our twisted made up Christianity, but not the Christianity in its essence. Unfortunately, there is a minority that sees all the stupidity and absurdity of today’s society and religion and only a few of them who will speak about it. So, speak. Don’t end it with this book. Keep on writing. Please.<br />I laughed when I came to this part: <br />“and I dare the priest that can look down to a sinner and say;<br />‘your sins are forgiven’<br />to do the same with his daughter after she has had an abortion…” Double LOL. You should see our priests here. :D Lovely outfit, though. <br />Well said, of course. I imagined that situation. That’s what we, the believers, the people, the citizens allowed a long time ago. Instead of letting the inquisitors slay us we should have slain them. We are the mass and we behave as if we are one ignorant mortal individual. Everything’s so wrong in this world. <br />I felt the pain because I realized that we are the zombies, brainless machines and Facebook nation that are programmed to repeat the same activity every day. That’s bad… That’s why the everyday news are negative, black, bloody. One individual is an important part of a mass, but as an individual one has no value. But if one should make the first step and make another one listen, then maybe something changes. Maybe then we’ll understand the unconditional love. <br />Yes, the end of the book. You made it very clear that you don’t want to make profit with the book. Anyway, my copy of “The Unwords” is a present from the UnAuthor, so it misses the end. Thank you once again for the (un)words and confidence. I will spread the unwords… <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5625998569786842539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_319735049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319735049" />
    <a title="B.  Barron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2532066-b-barron"><img alt="B.  Barron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507277316p2/2532066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319735049?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B.  Barron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B.  Barron" href="/user/show/2532066-b-barron">B.  Barron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2532066-b-barron?shelf=ebook-online">ebook-online</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2532066-b-barron?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319735049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15091588521514515213">The author (The pseudonymous unauthor) gave me a copy of the first chapter of his book (Titled “Aesthetics”). I am a huge fan of both pseudonymous people (Gee, wonder why that is?) and free stuff, so despite the fact that I am a poetry plebeian (High poetry for me usually consist of limericks who's first line ends in 'Nantucket') I gave it a go.<br/><br/>At first I thought it was good. Not spectacular, not great – but solid poetry that didn’t quite catch me. Combining that with the art, which is also good</span>
  <span id="freeText15091588521514515213" style="display:none">The author (The pseudonymous unauthor) gave me a copy of the first chapter of his book (Titled “Aesthetics”). I am a huge fan of both pseudonymous people (Gee, wonder why that is?) and free stuff, so despite the fact that I am a poetry plebeian (High poetry for me usually consist of limericks who's first line ends in 'Nantucket') I gave it a go.<br /><br />At first I thought it was good. Not spectacular, not great – but solid poetry that didn’t quite catch me. Combining that with the art, which is also good but seemed at first like a declaration of “See how clever and talented and deep I am. Don't you wish you were half as good as I?” I was not displeased, but not amazed.<br /><br />Then I reached the line:<br /><br />“A chemotherapy for loneliness...”<br /><br />And I thought, clever. I kind of like that.<br /><br />And then I read:<br /><br />“Where death's speed is a thousand lives per second...”<br /><br />And I though, Damn! That’s good!<br /><br />And from that point on I was enthralled. <br /><br />My biggest complaint, well complaints as they are three-fold:<br />1) €10.00 ($13) for a 90 page paperback is a little steep, for I am cheep (ode to my love of limericks).<br />2) I am nervous ordering from sites I am unfamiliar with. Call me crazy, call me paranoid, call me Ishmael. I wish the author would allow Amazon or Barns &amp; Noble or someone. And yes, he is using Paypal which goes a long way to alleviating my concerns – so I will probably shell out the case at some point regardless of my misgivings. It just make me.... cautions.<br />3) Being a techno-geek I wish he had a Kindle version for sale. Yes, I do love and prefer the physical book BUT I am really developing a love for the e-reader.<br /><br />So I give this incomplete review a solid 4 as I try and scrape together some spare cash.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15091588521514515213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_417685106" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer17564629933775552350">An exquisite and thought - provoking read! As George Orwell said, “In a time of deceit, telling the truth is a revolutionary act”. This is precisely what the author of The Unwords is trying to achieve. A revolution in our perception of the world! By using honesty as his most powerful weapon, he pushes us out of our comfort zone and attempts to change our way of thinking ones and for all.<br/><br/>Nowadays the society is structured in such a way that ethics and humanity are becoming slowly extinct. The aut</span>
  <span id="freeText17564629933775552350" style="display:none">An exquisite and thought - provoking read! As George Orwell said, “In a time of deceit, telling the truth is a revolutionary act”. This is precisely what the author of The Unwords is trying to achieve. A revolution in our perception of the world! By using honesty as his most powerful weapon, he pushes us out of our comfort zone and attempts to change our way of thinking ones and for all.<br /><br />Nowadays the society is structured in such a way that ethics and humanity are becoming slowly extinct. The author of The Unwords throws a punch in the face of the system and introduces a new approach to the way we see others and ourselves.<br /><br />This book is a mind-stretching meditation which makes us wonder: “What if the world didn't work the way it does now?” Maybe it’s time for a whole new perspective. Truly recommended!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11630049292860048378">Wow....<br/>.0000000000000000000000000000000001 stars.<br/>This book aimed for profundity and landed on naïveté. The writing reads like the vague ramblings of an 18 year old who believes his mind has been opened, all of the posers have been exposed, and that this 18 year old alone has all of the answers to the world's problems.<br/>Yeah.   <span id="freeText11630049292860048378" style="display:none">Wow....<br />.0000000000000000000000000000000001 stars.<br />This book aimed for profundity and landed on naïveté. The writing reads like the vague ramblings of an 18 year old who believes his mind has been opened, all of the posers have been exposed, and that this 18 year old alone has all of the answers to the world's problems.<br />Yeah. No.<br />I downloaded this book because I am interested in exploring the way ebook forms can combine many mediums. In this way, Unwords is interesting, but still not a success. The use of contrasting colors and bold font does not a profound statement make.<br />This book read like something written by The Underground Man. However, instead of recognizing its absurdity, Unwords seems to be taken with its own assumed profundity (which, I restate, is absent). Unfortunately, instead of revealing the gag, the commitment to a created, absurd character, the introduction instead confirmed my feeling that the author truly believes he has done something marvelously profound in this book.</span>

<div id="review_804322702" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/804322702" />
    <a title="Sheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1225564-sheryl"><img alt="Sheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539053038p2/1225564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/804322702?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheryl" href="/user/show/1225564-sheryl">Sheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789963746712" href="/book/show/18186565-the-unwords">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer804322702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12124467155297913069">A graphic novel in verse - two literary forms for which I don't care much, but decided to give a try. The writing is not bad, particularly as verse goes, but the content? Ugh. UGH. Arrogant, angry, pessimistic and dark. Get the writer some drugs and remove all sharp objects from his sight. Nothing good ever existed in the world and everyone sucks, especially you, you selfish corporate drone completely controlled by big business and big government (note: this means YOU, unless you are the writer)</span>
  <span id="freeText12124467155297913069" style="display:none">A graphic novel in verse - two literary forms for which I don't care much, but decided to give a try. The writing is not bad, particularly as verse goes, but the content? Ugh. UGH. Arrogant, angry, pessimistic and dark. Get the writer some drugs and remove all sharp objects from his sight. Nothing good ever existed in the world and everyone sucks, especially you, you selfish corporate drone completely controlled by big business and big government (note: this means YOU, unless you are the writer). It is exactly this type of persona (which may or may not be indicative of the actual author's worldview) that defines the stereotype of the moody, artsy, dirty hippie (which is a hurtful, untrue stereotype). If, indeed, this work is a fiction mocking the persona, bravo. If it is the angsty writing of an actual human's beliefs, I hope they call their doctor to get treated for a nasty case of depression. <br /><br />These were my thoughts before I read the afterword at the end of the book. I very much appreciated understanding where the author was coming from for a couple of reasons:<br /><br />1. My American bias shows terribly in my reaction. I have never had to withstand the kind of socio-political environment the author experienced growing up. <br /><br />2. The author pretty much cops to feeling exactly how I described him: Arrogant, angry, pessimistic and dark. However, he feels he has moved beyond it. Based both on the work and the afterword, I disagree. I still see tremendous anger, pessimism and arrogance. <br /><br />That said, the literary effort and the artistic impulse are driven by passion, and rarely does a book make me feel so strongly. Given the highly personal nature of the work, I hesitate to respond with such a negative response, but my emotions are every bit as valid as the authors, so I will leave with an honest review: I really didn't like the work and wouldn't recommend it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12124467155297913069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Vik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/327086-vik"><img alt="Vik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352330864p2/327086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vik" href="/user/show/327086-vik">Vik</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/327086-vik?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/327086-vik?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297838788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10409951048439851013">I absolutely loved this, verse was never this good when I did English lit many many moons ago or would be a big fan of poetry now. This will challenge your conceptions on certain topics and the religious iconography may not be to everyone's taste but you can't please everyone.<br/><br/>Overall the book is split into 3 themed sections and it flows so well, you can feel the different emotions that are being evoked and I felt connected to the unwords. The ending is a surprise, albeit a pleasant one, I hope p</span>
  <span id="freeText10409951048439851013" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this, verse was never this good when I did English lit many many moons ago or would be a big fan of poetry now. This will challenge your conceptions on certain topics and the religious iconography may not be to everyone's taste but you can't please everyone.<br /><br />Overall the book is split into 3 themed sections and it flows so well, you can feel the different emotions that are being evoked and I felt connected to the unwords. The ending is a surprise, albeit a pleasant one, I hope people discover this for themselves as per the unauthor's request. <br /><br />Get hold of a copy today, you won't regret it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10409951048439851013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_734442532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/734442532" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/734442532?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789963746712" href="/book/show/18186565-the-unwords">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer734442532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9986818729599395372">`There is nothing more dangerous than a character with no author.'<br/><br/>Non Nomen (`no name') is the moniker assigned by the author to provide his anonymity, but that at first seemingly gimmick to sell a book should in no way deter readers from delving into this collection of thoughts and images and poetry that has the courage to `unleash a full scale attack on all fronts of cultural and social decay.' What we learn from his introduction is that he grew up in a `very violent, ultra-nationalistic, drug</span>
  <span id="freeText9986818729599395372" style="display:none">`There is nothing more dangerous than a character with no author.'<br /><br />Non Nomen (`no name') is the moniker assigned by the author to provide his anonymity, but that at first seemingly gimmick to sell a book should in no way deter readers from delving into this collection of thoughts and images and poetry that has the courage to `unleash a full scale attack on all fronts of cultural and social decay.' What we learn from his introduction is that he grew up in a `very violent, ultra-nationalistic, drug-filled social environment. There was a military camp right nest to my school but not a single library within a 30 mile radius.' His family was warm and supportive in severe contrast to the outside world and he found solace in painting at a very young age. Impressed by the Alan Moore book `V for Vendetta' his perception of what world around him changed. `It sparked a need for justice and a thirst for knowledge and rebellion.' He combined his art with his writings and the ultimate result of many years of gestation was this book.<br /><br />To `review' a book of this nature borders on the impossible, other than to encourage people to read it for themselves and respond viscerally as well as artistically and intellectually. The design of the book is splendid; each page is covered with the author's art or manipulations of imagery that serve as the matrix for his words. The book is divided into three sections: Aesthetics, The Discipline of the Watch, and A Thankless Task. An excerpt from the first section follows:<br /><br />A smile,<br />compressed and encrypted.<br /><br />A touch,<br />password protected.<br /><br />You passed my by today.<br /><br />You went by me so swift,<br />in such a hurry.<br />like an empty promise<br />eager to be ignored;<br />to be forgotten<br /><br />Why won't you look at me<br />and welcome me into your world?<br />It's so easy.<br />A smile, a split of a second a word...<br />yet so expensive.<br /><br />I miss the kisses I haven't given you yet.<br />I miss the memories we haven't shared yet.<br />I still miss you...<br />yet.<br /><br />This rather restrained and tender poem is like the match that lights the blaze that follows - poems of dissection of our moral fiber, our sense of emptiness we have created, our isolation. The works are at times tough to read because they sting. But they deserve to be read and digested and Non Nomen presents that need. He serves attention. <br /><br />Grady Harp</span>
  <a data-text-id="9986818729599395372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309761612" />
    <a title="Zoey42" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6006765-zoey42"><img alt="Zoey42" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331039829p2/6006765.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309761612?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoey42" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoey42" href="/user/show/6006765-zoey42">Zoey42</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6006765-zoey42?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309761612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2385127705696905979">I received the book for free through <b>Goodreads First Reads</b> and at first I wasn't sure about this book. I thought there are so many people out there who love reading poetry and philosophy books, but it isn't my cup of tea. Really. <br/><br/>Boy, I was totally wrong. At the moment I got the book, I read the book in one day. It left my mind blown and I couldn't sort out my thoughts, so the next day I read it again, that time more slowly, carefully thinking over each verse.<br/><br/>Some people find this book revolutio</span>
  <span id="freeText2385127705696905979" style="display:none">I received the book for free through <b>Goodreads First Reads</b> and at first I wasn't sure about this book. I thought there are so many people out there who love reading poetry and philosophy books, but it isn't my cup of tea. Really. <br /><br />Boy, I was totally wrong. At the moment I got the book, I read the book in one day. It left my mind blown and I couldn't sort out my thoughts, so the next day I read it again, that time more slowly, carefully thinking over each verse.<br /><br />Some people find this book revolutionary. I feel 'The Unwords' is about things you've already known. It just helps you realize that there are some issues in today's world which are not right and we all should think about what we could change in our society... <br /><br />P.S.: This book has one of the most beautiful design I've ever seen, the pictures and painting are truly amazing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2385127705696905979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6690843245097968818">I got The Unwords because it was free on Amazon.com. From the title I expected it was a discourse on the use and misuse of language in our culture. That's not what it is.<br/><br/>One thing that is unusual about this book is that almost every page is written on a graphic, and image of some sort.   <span id="freeText6690843245097968818" style="display:none">I got The Unwords because it was free on Amazon.com. From the title I expected it was a discourse on the use and misuse of language in our culture. That's not what it is.<br /><br />One thing that is unusual about this book is that almost every page is written on a graphic, and image of some sort. This is the first time I've seen this on my Kindle. That's the best part of this book.<br /><br />The author is unknown, anonymous, Non Nomen. The author has a damaged, dismal outlook. She resents her parents.<br /><br />The text is written in the format of poetry. It is poetry-like, poetoid. Quasi-verse, pseudo-verse. Unverse.</span>

Thoughts that have become taboo only through the social assimilation that every person wishes not to recognize in themselves. Contemplating themself, and everyone else coexisting (or lack thereof) on this planet we call ea</span>
  <span id="freeText8445940334273778699" style="display:none">The Unwords brings a philosophically provocative point of view. The definition of the title seems to be the unspoken. Thoughts that have become taboo only through the social assimilation that every person wishes not to recognize in themselves. From the trauma of psychological isolation to the social acceptance of blame, every word echoes the nearly six years the author has taken to compile this book. Contemplating themself, and everyone else coexisting (or lack thereof) on this planet we call earth, and this reality we call home. -Stephany</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7393848122610615856">I received "The Unwords" in the mail today. I started reading it just to see what it was really about and I didn't put it down until I finished it. "The Unwords" is an exquisitely poetic tale which takes the reader on an unusual journey through the facts of the world we live in that we often don't acknowledge. I'm sure I'll read this multiple times. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16406496995313987701">I'm really not certain what to make of this book - self-righteous and arrogant, angsty and personal. It doesn't really seem like poetry (it is far too straightforward) but it is written in poetic form, with art that I also don't know what to make of. I will give it a second read to see if I can make up my mind. </span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qvXAkdTueusKRiUunc9S5oLnaJ8MXmsKNKNZL9L+Sdv+6e2fl3RtXpuMR++ykvMEHQsJmqMT/au1nxhf/O6RcQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hJRixtYDvr+flDneptdRPqad0dRmC0DYGJcvTNmNLRzQiE/IlZmpCg5eWx+JivDcOXGw0clG1nmZq2489531tg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9241514011076110541">Non Nomen is latin for "no name." Due to the author's anonymity, biographical information is limited to his British/Cypriot nationality. He uses a very distinctive method of writing known as Graphic-verse.<br/> <br/>His debut, entitled The Unwords, was first published in January 2012 (limited edition). A Goodreads Choice Award Finalist the same year, the limited edition of The Unwords became notorious for i</span>
  <span id="freeText9241514011076110541" style="display:none">Non Nomen is latin for "no name." Due to the author's anonymity, biographical information is limited to his British/Cypriot nationality. He uses a very distinctive method of writing known as Graphic-verse.<br /> <br />His debut, entitled The Unwords, was first published in January 2012 (limited edition). A Goodreads Choice Award Finalist the same year, the limited edition of The Unwords became notorious for its highly unorthodox final page. The second edition of The Unwords was released in July 2013 and received wide distribution in the US and the UK, eventually reaching a #1 Amazon Bestseller status in its category.<br /> <br />His next publication, entitled Bury Me in Her Eyes, was released in February 2015. With 28 different languages interrelating within its content, the book is rightfully considered the first multilingual literary work ever written. Non Nomen officially became a Guinness World Record Holder on January 19th, 2015 and the only English translation of Bury Me in Her Eyes (the Newtonian edition) can be found in the Rare Books Collection of Cambridge University. Bury Me in Her Eyes struggled to find an audience due to its unconventional linguistic structure, but it has become the author's most critically acclaimed work, having received high praise within the academic circles.<br /> <br />His next project, entitled Logos, is still in development, with no official release date.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9241514011076110541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
